  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c8f20c78-ab48-4994-9bda-45011a0d8ecc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText12245201307820097854" style="display:none">A new series of global proportions -- from master of intrigue, NEW YORK TIMES bestselling author Ally Carter.<br /><br />Grace Blakely is absolutely certain of three things:<br /><br />1. She is not crazy.<br />2. Her mother was murdered.<br />3. Someday she is going to find the killer and make him pay.<br /><br />As certain as Grace is about these facts, nobody else believes her -- so there's no one she can completely trust. Not her grandfather, a powerful ambassador. Not her new friends, who all live on Embassy Row. Not Alexei, the Russian boy next door, who is keeping his eye on Grace for reasons she neither likes nor understands.<br /><br />Everybody wants Grace to put on a pretty dress and a pretty smile, blocking out all her unpretty thoughts. But they can't control Grace -- no more than Grace can control what she knows or what she needs to do. Her past has come back to hunt her . . . and if she doesn't stop it, Grace isn't the only one who will get hurt. Because on Embassy Row, the countries of the world stand like dominoes, and one wrong move can make them all fall down.</span>

<div id="review_3357101066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3357101066" />
    <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader"><img alt="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550626778p2/8114361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3357101066?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader">Jesse (JesseTheReader)</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3357101066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13249243225267101576">I randomly picked this up off my shelves the other day and plowed my way through it pretty quickly. There are definitely things within this book that you have to suspend your disbelief for, because some things that go down are a bit outlandish. I loved the group of characters that form to work together on breaking down the mystery at hand and the plot went in such a unexpected direction that left me pleasantly surprised. I will say that there is a major over use of the word crazy... could've tak</span>
  <span id="freeText13249243225267101576" style="display:none">I randomly picked this up off my shelves the other day and plowed my way through it pretty quickly. There are definitely things within this book that you have to suspend your disbelief for, because some things that go down are a bit outlandish. I loved the group of characters that form to work together on breaking down the mystery at hand and the plot went in such a unexpected direction that left me pleasantly surprised. I will say that there is a major over use of the word crazy... could've taken out 50 and we would've gotten the point. Overall though, this was entertaining and I'll definitely be working my way through the trilogy! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13249243225267101576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1681063379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1681063379" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1681063379?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=originality">originality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1681063379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16025508350614749545"><i>All Fall Down</i> may not be Ally Carter’s best work, but it’s still, as always with this author, darn fast-paced, entertaining and original.<br/><br/>The moment I started reading it, I was sucked into the world of ambassadors and soirées and danger. <br/><br/>Grace lost her mom. Correction—her mom was murdered. They all say it was an accident, but Grace knows the truth.<br/><br/>She was there.<br/><br/>And she knows who killed her.<br/><br/>She wants to make him pay, and she will.<br/><br/>I found the whole concept of ambassadors from all over the world who</span>
  <span id="freeText16025508350614749545" style="display:none"><i>All Fall Down</i> may not be Ally Carter’s best work, but it’s still, as always with this author, darn fast-paced, entertaining and original.<br /><br />The moment I started reading it, I was sucked into the world of ambassadors and soirées and danger. <br /><br />Grace lost her mom. Correction—her mom was murdered. They all say it was an accident, but Grace knows the truth.<br /><br />She was there.<br /><br />And she knows who killed her.<br /><br />She wants to make him pay, and she will.<br /><br />I found the whole concept of ambassadors from all over the world who live next to one another—on a street called ‘‘Embassy Row’’—very unique. I never read anything similar to it.<br /><br />Sure, the mystery and murder lacked complexity—usually, with a murder, we have multiple suspects, but in this book, it’s limited to one. Therefore, it’s more suspenseful than mysterious.<br /><br />I nonetheless felt unspeakably engaged into the story, despite the immaturity of the characters, the lackluster romance and, as I said, the limited mystery to the murder of Grace’s mother.<br /><br />Ally Carter knows how to write a book in a way that will make the reader not want to stop reading. Her chapters are not too long, her writing is simple—maybe too simple—and her characters fun and somewhat relatable, though sadly I personally cannot relate to (slightly) immature teens.<br /><br />I’m usually not that interested in reading the sequel to a book I only gave three stars to, but that’s exactly how I feel right now.<br /><br />The story ends on a huge cliffhanger, so you’ll want to have the next book beside you after you’re done with this one. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16025508350614749545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1059804286" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059804286" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17389678-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145890p2/17389678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059804286?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/17389678-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780545654784" href="/book/show/18115187-all-fall-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=books-that-spark-national-treasure">books-that-spark-national-treasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=gimme-2015-k">gimme-2015-k</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=i-d-give-you-the-stars">i-d-give-you-the-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059804286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer400990425137010789"><blockquote>
  <b> Diplomacy, ambiguity and a hot Russian love interest. Sorry, Jess will have to get back to you. She’s currently nursing her book hangover. </b>
</blockquote> <br/>I know my last review was all about the book of my dreams and whatnot, but <i>All Fall Down</i> was basically an element of reality that I'm quite close to and the best that imagination can offer and it's made me wonder<i> “Why weren’t you creative enough to dream that up, Jess?”</i> Now I don’t want to get ahead of myself here, seeing as it’s only January and all, b</span>
  <span id="freeText400990425137010789" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b> Diplomacy, ambiguity and a hot Russian love interest. Sorry, Jess will have to get back to you. She’s currently nursing her book hangover. </b>
</blockquote> <br>I know my last review was all about the book of my dreams and whatnot, but <i>All Fall Down</i> was basically an element of reality that I'm quite close to and the best that imagination can offer and it's made me wonder<i> “Why weren’t you creative enough to dream that up, Jess?”</i> Now I don’t want to get ahead of myself here, seeing as it’s only January and all, but that may have been the best book I’ve read in a long while. Alright, so since last week. But as you can see, I’m rather smitten by this book. Because it combined a concept that I know all too well about together with the <b>joys of the thriller genre and an ounce of conspiracy. </b><br><br>We all know that I’m weak with the contemporary. Truthfully, I’m weak with all contemporaries but one. While I detest those sob fests (I can’t connect) that are meant to mirror life and all its imperfections and whatnot, I adore contemporary thrillers. Because I like murder tales. Not the murder (oh joy, here’s my murder disclaimer once again. I don’t like murder. I’m just interested by the thrill of the chase for justice.) <b>Ally Carter does something that has yet to be touched in YA. Which is a feat in itself, because what out there hasn’t been given the YA makeover. </b>Embassy kiddies and a murder mystery. Sign me up. <br><br>Fun fact: January 2015 was only ever about two books for me. Conspiracy of Us and All Fall Down. Reading for this month is pretty much complete for me. In between waiting for the two, I’ve been slumping. Nothing’s been holding my attention. But these two, I devoured them in a matter of hours. I inflated my own expectations. They exceeded it. 2015 has been good to me, thus far. <br><br>Ally Carter presents us with Grace. Child of a dead mother and deployed military father. Sent of to live with her Grandfather, US ambassador, stationed in Adria. It’s all about diplomacy on Embassy Row. The thing with embassies is, they’re always clumped together. And seeing as each block of land is representative of the nation itself, tensions are always high around the embassy blocks. One wrong step, one mistake on foreign soil and it’s an international scandal.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “We must respect our host country and we must respect our neighbours.”… “Sometimes the walls that stand between us and our neighbours are all that stand between our country and war.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br>Grace hasn’t been back on embassy row since her mother was murdered right before her eyes. And now she’s plagued with a bunch of memories that she’d much rather forget and a desire to bring justice to her mother, to defend her honour, to unearth her killer—the Scarred Man. Only, the thing with being a kid is that you’re less likely to gain respect. Especially from a adults who are trained, and who base their career off being vague, politically correct and morally ambiguous (your country first, and if anything disastrous should happen, your country should assume a facade of innocence). <br><br>The portrayal of Embassy Row is completely on point. While it’s all manners and polite and courteous smiles, the air is tense. One step out of line and it’s a domino effect. Carter builds this atmosphere with utter delicacy. I adored it. I’m a tad skeptical of the fact that you can be posted in one country for so long (it’s a moving job), but hey, that’s fiction. You gotta give a little leeway and let the imagination take over, right? <br><br>We follow Grace’s journey as she attempts to prove her credibility. As a character, I adored her. We get an <b>extremely unreliable narrator,</b> which may do a couple of heads in, but to me, it added to the charm of <i>All Fall Down</i>. The book is littered with what appears to be flashbacks, but as we proceed, it becomes rather blurry and hard to differentiate between flashback and hallucination. Grace’s sass, however, won over my heart. Holy hell, that girl is just perfectly sarcastic. What segregates me from YA protagonists, and often becomes a barrier for empathy, is the fact that many of our protagonists are rather submissive. Which isn’t a bad trait. But it’s just hard for me to personally understand. <b>Grace isn’t demure and shy, she doesn’t lack confidence and fear the spotlight. </b>Which is something that I’ve been searching for in a protagonist. Because if they’re meant to be a reflection of the young adult, it’s a rather one dimensional view of us. I don’t want to speak on anybody else’s behalf but man, I used (sometimes still ha!) to think I could own the world. And there was no way I was going to let someone else topple me over. She’s got sass and now that I’ve had a taste of it, I demand more.<br><br>We’ve also got a great selection of secondary characters. They’re all rather individual, and I believe that with time, and the following sequels, their backstories will surely be developed in greater detail. There are two males named. I mention that because everyone likes to jump ahead and toot the big love triangle horn. <b>There is no love triangle</b>. There is one potential love interest and a newly acquired best friend. Noah is an absolutely hilarious and rather endearing character. He’s the type that just grows on you. He’s a perfect contrast to Grace’s characterisation, and a fantastic friend. While she is plagued with mystery and ambiguity, he is all about clarity and a dose of reality. And a complete sweetheart. <br><br>Those who are familiar with Carter’s work will know that she does love extremely lightly. <i>All Fall Down</i> does not stray away from that pattern. Carter knows a thing or two about slow burn, let me tell you. She’ll let you burn on forever and you’ll be begging for a something—a sign, a touch, a look. That also translates to: <b>Grace, our protagonist, does not use love to procrastinate from her mission for justice. She does not fall prey to transcendental love. </b>For our little Gracie here, we have Alexei. Yes, a Russian kiddie. <b>You should all know that I have two week spots in life: royalty and Russian men.</b> While we got both elements in this one, Alexei completely whisked me away. Brother’s best friend. That’s who he is. <b>And between the bit of witty banter shared between the two and the fact that he’s a complete gentlemen, I’m kind of sold. </b>I told you, Carter knows her slow burn. <br><br>The thing with Carter is, she does simplistic writing. But it’s extremely addictive. It’s a formula that I’ve yet to read elsewhere. Normally I like my writing with a bounty of obscure metaphors (I’m kind of partial to those) and lyricism that would surely drive you all up the wall, but when it comes to Carter, I give that Jess a break. Because Carter’s writing always has me hooked.<b> She knows her dialogue, she knows how to describe actions and movements and secret glances with absolute accuracy.</b> It’s all about realism when it comes to her writing. Her dialogue is always extremely witty, which is something that I love. And her scenes transition with fantastic fluidity. So forget the metaphors, for once in your life. Carter knows how to sell the whole<i> “less is more”</i> idea. <br><br>Be warned though, with the conclusion to <i>All Fall Down</i> one thing for sure is that this series is heading down a completely different direction. One that I’ve been screaming at YA to do for a while. So I’m totally alright with it all. I won’t say much about it, just because you’ve got to experience it for yourself (although, some may just know, now that I’ve been all vague and whatnot). Carter may have my soul because I want that second book. <br><br>Basically <i>All Fall Down</i> has ruined me. It pulled me out of my slump, gave me the best story of my life (an element—not the murder—of this book hits home for me, so be warned, like all things, this may not be for everyone), and has now said, see you in 2016 kiddo. Carter brings forth a completely delicate and precarious setting and places a protagonist who is willing to burrow for the truth at the heart of it. Things get shaken up in this delectable read. Jess reads too deeply into the interactions of two certain characters (and hopes that Carter will give her more to work with in book two). <i>All Fall Down</i> has stolen my heart, and head, for the rest of January, if not the rest of the year. Read it for a breath of fresh air. Read it for a slow burning romance. Read it for the impeccable cast. I guess this review came sooner than later. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b> Can everyone do me a favour and just read this book? Carter has my heart. You know the deal, <u>review to come. </u></b>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406175072ra/10514889.gif" width="400" height="354" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I, of all people, had the most inflated expectations out there. I hyped this one up for myself, based on blurb alone. That's right, I did the unthinkable, the <i>no-no</i> when it comes to highly anticipated books. Guess what? Expectations met <i>and exceeded</i>. I am one happy duck right here. Plus, there's a lovely Russian love interest and y'all know how I get when that happens. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385341680ra/7129146.gif" width="250" height="145" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="400990425137010789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1076068929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1076068929" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1076068929?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1076068929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9224897592992043951"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> All Fall Down </b> is my first Ally Carter book and I must say, it's an enjoyable read. The age level is a little lower than I usually read, I would classify this book as a middle grade for ages 12-16. It is the perfect type of book for transitioning young readers out of the chapter books and into the Young Adult/Teen genre.<br/><br/>Three years after witnessing her mother's death Grace is sent to live with her ambassador grandfather in a country that borders Iran. Grace used to spend her summers </span>
  <span id="freeText9224897592992043951" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br /><br /><b> All Fall Down </b> is my first Ally Carter book and I must say, it's an enjoyable read. The age level is a little lower than I usually read, I would classify this book as a middle grade for ages 12-16. It is the perfect type of book for transitioning young readers out of the chapter books and into the Young Adult/Teen genre.<br /><br />Three years after witnessing her mother's death Grace is sent to live with her ambassador grandfather in a country that borders Iran. Grace used to spend her summers at the embassy as a child and is already familiar with the area and the politics. While here, Grace discovers that the man she believes to have murdered her mother is here as well, and she sets about on a plan to bring him down.<br /><br />This is one of the more interesting plots I've read in the young adult genre, lots of modern day politics and espionage are afoot. I'm not really used to reading a simpler type of book and that's why this book received a 3.5 star review from me. Plus, I found the ending to be highly unbelievable.<br /><br />I think many teens, girls and boys, could relate very well to Grace and her situation. No, not all teens are able to deal with inter-political plots between countries, but they will relate to Grace and her struggle for adults to take her seriously. The adults in this book did not believe Grace when she went to them for help, leaving her feeling useless and helpless, something many teens feel like a lot of the time. I liked that Grace did what most teens (and people) want to do, and she took matters into her own hands and tried to unravel the mystery of her mother's death herself.<br /><br />I would have liked more development between Grace and the character of Alexei. I still at this point cannot determine if he was a love interest or not. He just sort of popped in and then would disappear for various amounts of time. It felt really random. Hopefully that will be resolved in the next installment.<br /><br /><i> ARC kindly provided to me by my boss. Who received this from the publisher. So I guess the ARC was indeed provided by the publisher. It just wasn't intended for me. Muahaha! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9224897592992043951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_919892326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/919892326" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/919892326?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781743628942" href="/book/show/24830401-all-fall-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=grinned-like-a-fool">grinned-like-a-fool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=swoony-guys">swoony-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=me-likes-you">me-likes-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer919892326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6294795270898360177">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Being someone who hasn't read anything by Ally Carter before, I went into this book... not expecting all that much. But knowing that Ms. Carter's previous books have all been something along the lines of a mystery thriller-y espionage kinda thing, let me assure you now, this isn't anything like that. Heck, this book is definitely something that I wouldn't think you've picked up beforehand. It's original right to it's roots.<strong> <em>All Fall Down </em>combines a w</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText6294795270898360177" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Being someone who hasn't read anything by Ally Carter before, I went into this book... not expecting all that much. But knowing that Ms. Carter's previous books have all been something along the lines of a mystery thriller-y espionage kinda thing, let me assure you now, this isn't anything like that. Heck, this book is definitely something that I wouldn't think you've picked up beforehand. It's original right to it's roots.<strong> <em>All Fall Down </em>combines a world of diplomacy and the repercussions of death into one fun mess--I told you this wasn't like anything you've read before.</strong><br /><br /><strong>Grace Blakely is one of those characters you really wanna love and sympathise with.</strong> She lost her mother at the age of 13 and she was there to see it happen. Grace doesn't even get to see her father or brother anymore because they're both away on duty as they're soldiers. And her grandfather? He's the US Ambassador and now Grace has to live with him in Adria. It also happens to be the place where her mother was murdered right in front of her eyes. Not that anyone would believe Grace, for they all say the death was an accident.<br /><br /><strong>My first impression on Ally Carter was that she's a genius.</strong> A GENIUS, I TELL YOU. Why? Because I absolutely loved the idea of a place where all the embassy houses happen to be on the same street and for each step you make, you could be visiting the other side of the world. For instance, the Russian embassy is next door to the US embassy. Take a step out of the US half and BAM you're basically in Russia. I mean, we have embassies in existence in the real world but to incorporate it into a story line? I repeat, GENIUS. Though, I would recommend people to have some understanding of embassies and how they work in our world before heading into this book, because I imagine it can be a little confusing at the start for some when nothing is yet explained.<br /><br />Anyway, back to Grace. *coughs* I totally didn't get carried away there. *coughs again* I wanted to love the girl. Her situation is pretty unfortunate and well, witnessing your own mother's death? That's just unimaginably horrific and traumatic. But, <strong>Grace turned out to be a really annoying girl who loved to jump to conclusions instead.</strong> I mean, there's this scene where Grace comes across a girl who's got a pretty face and seems to hold an authoritative voice, and Grace seems to just loose all reason and starts going on and on about how that chick must be one of <em>those </em>kind of girls. Like what the hell? You just met her!<br /><br />What I did expect to see in <em>All Fall Down </em>was a romance. I don't know how that idea got into my brain but... all YA novels seem to have romances these days, so I guess I automatically drilled that into my mind. ANYWAY.<strong> There isn't necessarily a romance in this book.</strong> While I can foresee one appearing in the future instalments, this book was purely character and plot driven. I do believe Alexei is supposed to be the love interest. I mean, hello? Hot Russian dude? Personally, I wasn't a fan of him. <strong>He has this cold demeanor and he's so domineering.</strong> I barely understood the guy, honestly. <strong>BUT, then there's Noah. *squees* HE'S MIIIIIINE.</strong> He's half Israeli and half Brazillian. He spends half his time in the Israel embassy and the rest in the Brazillian embassy. It's pretty awesome if you ask me. And what else is awesome? The fact that Noah is a totally adorable and sweet guy who has the best humour and made me chuckle on multiple occasions. <strong>Can I please have a Noah too? </strong><br /><blockquote>'OK,' he says. 'First lesson.'<br />Noah broadens his stance, taking his place firmly on the embassy side of the threshold. 'In the United States,' he says. Then, with both feet, he leaps on to the sidewalk. 'Out of the United States.' Quickly, he jumps back toward me. 'In the United States.' Another jump across the threshold. 'Out of the United States. In. Out. In --'<br />'Is this the part where I hit you?'</blockquote><br /><strong>Other than that, I would've liked to see more political involvement in this book.</strong> I'm not sure if I'm being just plain picky here but I love love loved the whole embassy idea being presented in a novel, and taking it up a notch in the upcoming instalments would be very much appreciated, because I can see that Ms. Carter definitely has to skills to make it work.<br /><br /><strong>If you want a fun and quick read with a little more substance and politics than your typical lighthearted contemporary, this is one I'd highly recommend. </strong><br /><p>
  <em>~Thank you Scholastic Australia for sending me this copy!~</em>
</p></span>

<div id="review_892750179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892750179" />
    <a title="Marga " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6418118-marga"><img alt="Marga " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423326869p2/6418118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892750179?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marga " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marga " href="/user/show/6418118-marga">Marga </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22928735-all-fall-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=read-feb-2015">read-feb-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892750179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10079617027155176611">This review is also posted on <a href='http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>DEADLY DARLINGS.</a><br/><br/>Actual Rating: 3.5/5 stars<br/><br/><i>Grace saw her mother murdered right before her eyes but no one believes her.</i> They say it was an accident, that her mother was killed in the fire, but she knew the truth. Her mother was shot in the chest by a scarred man. But she was thirteen and they say that’s just trauma that’s talking so nobody believed her.<br/><br/>Anyway, she was back in Adria again after three years and decided to stay for good. In her stay, she discovered that</span>
  <span id="freeText10079617027155176611" style="display:none">This review is also posted on <a href="http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">DEADLY DARLINGS.</a><br /><br />Actual Rating: 3.5/5 stars<br /><br /><i>Grace saw her mother murdered right before her eyes but no one believes her.</i> They say it was an accident, that her mother was killed in the fire, but she knew the truth. Her mother was shot in the chest by a scarred man. But she was thirteen and they say that’s just trauma that’s talking so nobody believed her.<br /><br />Anyway, she was back in Adria again after three years and decided to stay for good. In her stay, she discovered that the man whom she believed killed her mother was here as well. So with the help of friends, she went to follow and observe this man and she felt really close now in figuring out what really happened in the night her mother died. Why did he kill her mother? <br /><br />Well, well, well. She definitely didn’t saw <i>that answers, that revelations</i> coming. <br /><br /><b>Lesson: </b>Sometimes, you just have to learn your boundaries, your limitations. We can never un-know things.<br /><br /><b>Maybe sometimes, ignorance is bliss.</b><br /><br /><i>I liked Grace, our heroine.</i> She was sarcastic and unafraid to speak her mind yet she was also fragile and really vulnerable. She was a very unreliable narrator. She started to doubt even herself when no one took her proclamations seriously and I actually felt sad for her. She felt really helpless and alone.<br /><br />I like the friendships in this book. Can I just say that I love Noah? He’s just adorable. He just introduced himself to Grace one day and said that he was her best friend. Anyway even though I liked the relationships here, it wasn’t perfect because it wasn’t developed enough. You know, this felt like a sort of introduction, like the author is just preparing us for more to come. Maybe we’ll see more of them in the next books.<br /><br /><b>The romance: </b><i>There’s not much room for romance here mainly because Grace wasn’t really in the right state for that.</i> She was lost and she felt a little crazy even. Anyway, I really think Alexei will be her love interest in this series even though he just sort of appeared here really randomly. I ship it! Their relationship is somewhat forbidden though because Alexei’s Russian and they’re nations aren’t really strong allies. At first, I thought there's a love triangle but there's none so yaay!<br /><br /><b>The Setting:</b> I loved the setting of this one! Embassy Row was literally like a lot of embassies next to each other, each representing a different country. Technically if you went to another side and you didn’t have permission, you can start a war between nations. I think Ally Carter can really expand this. There’s a lot of potential, there can be a lot of surprise villains and conspiracies and whatnots. I’m definitely looking forward to where she will bring this story.<br /><br />As a reader of works by Ally Carter before, I can definitely say that the first book is the somewhat the weakest in her series. Say for example, Gallagher Academy. But I also know that her books improve as the series goes on so I have no doubt that I will love the preceding installments even more than this. <br /><br /><i>*ARC provided by Netgalley in exchanged of an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10079617027155176611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          marked it as to-read


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780545654784" href="/book/show/18115187-all-fall-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=2015-january">2015-january</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=wishlist-maybe">wishlist-maybe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>

<div id="review_1091649118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1091649118" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1091649118?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780545654784" href="/book/show/18115187-all-fall-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=thriller-crime">thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091649118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14443307390621671715"><b>I am pleased</b>. I admit! I was dubious at the beginning! The first 100-pages didn't grab me...like, not at all. In fact, I was seriously wondering if this book would plummet into an untouchable basket. BUT THEN IT WOWED ME with a gob-smacking ending and some seriously wicked twists. I have a few quibbles, but overall I'm impressed.<br/><br/><b>It's not about spies! Or espionage!</b> I guess it's unfair to assume it will be, but Ally Carter has written <i>two</i> series about spies and crime, sooo, I guess it was my first</span>
  <span id="freeText14443307390621671715" style="display:none"><b>I am pleased</b>. I admit! I was dubious at the beginning! The first 100-pages didn't grab me...like, not at all. In fact, I was seriously wondering if this book would plummet into an untouchable basket. BUT THEN IT WOWED ME with a gob-smacking ending and some seriously wicked twists. I have a few quibbles, but overall I'm impressed.<br /><br /><b>It's not about spies! Or espionage!</b> I guess it's unfair to assume it will be, but Ally Carter has written <i>two</i> series about spies and crime, sooo, I guess it was my first assumption this would follow. IT DID NOT. It's set in a made up (?) country (I'm guess this is like Genova from <i>The Princess Diaries</i> right??) where there's an entire street of embassy houses. So Israel, Brazil, Russia, USA, etc. are all door-to-door. Technically when you visit a house, you're "in Russia" or whatnot. I'm <i>still</i> confused if it's an actual place or made up, though. <b>The story is about Grace, who's got PTSD after witnessing her mother's death.</b> She's convinced her was murdered by a scarred man. Basically she spends the entire book getting into raucous trouble, making bad decisions, snarking left-right-and-centre, and chasing after an elusive killer that <i>no one</i> but her believes is guilty.<br /><br /><b>I enjoyed Grace...but she also ticked me off.</b> I felt <i>bad</i> for her...I mean, she went through SO MUCH. But she really was a brat. She was a brat to everyone. But isn't that a coping mechanism?? So I feel bad judging her character, but...ugh, the rudenss did great on me.<br /><br />There are several secondary characters, and it's all very diverse (of course!) considering this is a row of Embassy houses. Like <br /><br />- <b> Noah:</b> who is half Israeli and half Brazilian...He elects himself Grace's Best Friend. It's adorable. HE'S HILARIOUS. <br />- <b> Alexei:</b> He's Russian and was Grace's older brother's friend in the past...and now kind of presents himself as the overbearing surrogate brother and Grace really gets ticked off by him (fair enough, too, Alexei was rather awful. He feigned caring but he called her "Gracie" when she specifically said not to, and he was very domineering.)<br />- <b>Megan:</b> She's like a computer genius.<br />- <b>Rosie:</b> She's a really smart 12 year old who knows everything, apparently, and is like a ninja when she sneaks after people.<br /><br /><b>I don't really think it has a love-triangle.</b> It has the <i>potential</i>, but I think <b>there was basically ZERO romance.</b> Which I'm glad about! Grace was definitely not in a position, mentally, to be having a romance. I loved Noah's very enthusiastic, charismatic friendship with her. Stuff Alexei.<br /><br /><b>The writing was fast and light...easy to read.</b> I kind of wish the author had aged the characters down, though, because the tone and content felt like 12+ friendly. The characters could've been 14. Seriously. They didn't seem excessively mature, either. And the book has literally no swearing.<br /><br /><b>So what are my quibbles?</b> Ergh. Unfortunately, I have a fair few. But some are spoilers, soooo I will wrap spoiler-tags as needed. <br /><br />- How rude and dismissive of everyone Grace was. She irritated me. A lot.<br />- That Noah and Grace have a "falling out' over the STUPIDEST THING EVER. And it's so cliche. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The whole "ooh you lied to me and now I hate you!" thing just drives me crazy. I thought Noah was better than that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- The fact that none of the girl characters were as fleshed out as the boys.<br />- How it portrayed getting counselling/medication in a very negative light.<br />- How the most common phrase was ARE YOU OKAY to Grace and nooo she's not. And if someone says "are you okay" again I'm going to freaking scream.<br />- The fact that when Grace has a falling out with one boy, she just flips to the other and everything is totally a-okay. It's just weird.<br />- When Graces comes to live in Embassy Row they stick her in her mother's old room...so it's full of her DEAD MUM'S STUFF. Um. Is this tasteless or is ti just me??? Grace is suffering serious trauma from witness her mother's death and yet they do this to her?? It's so wrong.<br />- Repetition...seriously everything was repeated. EVERYTHING. All the time. Lots of repetition. Do you know what I mean?? Gah. The dialogue felt so repetitious with the "I'm not crazy!" being Grace's every second phrase and little recaps on previous thoughts that were, um, really clear and didn't need recapping.<br /><br /><b>I enjoyed the book quite a bit!</b> It was a slow build-up to interest and the plot wasn't fast-paced, but it was engaging and the CLIFF HANGER, ERMAGERD. The end twist was quite shocking. I'm still sort of sitting here like a cod-fish with my mouth open. I have a <i>lot</i> of questions, but I think I'm supposed to (??) and they'll be answered later (??) I freaking hope. While I felt it was aimed at a definitely younger audience, I still enjoyed this!<br /><br />*whispers* I'm still seriously disappointed it's not crimey...<br /><br /><br /><b> NOTABLE QUOTES:</b><br /><br /><blockquote> "The obvious," Noah goes on, a little out of breath, "being that he is probably some super secret assassin or something. And I'm not as tough as I look."<br />"That's OK," I tell him. "I'm way tougher than you look." </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Ok," he says. "First lesson."<br />Noah broadens his stance, taking his place firmly on the embassy side of the threshold. "in the United States," he says. Then, with both feet, he leaps on to the sidewalk. "Out of the United States." Quickly, he jumps back toward me. "In the United States." Another jump across the threshold. "Out of the United States. In. Out. In --"<br />"Is this the part where I hit you?" </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14443307390621671715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678203377?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lainey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lainey" href="/user/show/22889537-lainey">Lainey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678203377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2957839585444373665">Actual Rating: 3.5/5<br/><br/>So I did really really enjoy this book. I wasn't sure what I was expecting going into this, but this was not what I was expecting at all (in a good way!)<br/><br/>I am really interested in YA Political Thrillers right now, so I picked this book up because of that. It is extremely easy to get through and it's fairly short. The reason I knocked off a star and a half is really simple:<br/><br/>Plot/Story > Characters.<br/><br/>I really liked this storyline and the mystery of it had me questioning everything.</span>
  <span id="freeText2957839585444373665" style="display:none">Actual Rating: 3.5/5<br /><br />So I did really really enjoy this book. I wasn't sure what I was expecting going into this, but this was not what I was expecting at all (in a good way!)<br /><br />I am really interested in YA Political Thrillers right now, so I picked this book up because of that. It is extremely easy to get through and it's fairly short. The reason I knocked off a star and a half is really simple:<br /><br />Plot/Story &gt; Characters.<br /><br />I really liked this storyline and the mystery of it had me questioning everything. Plus, our main character, Grace, is an unreliable narrator and I LOVED that, it even got me thinking and wondering if I was right or wrong. Now, with that being said, that was the only part of Grace's character I found complex. Her character as a whole was kind of... frustrating? I felt like she was 2-D 1/2, not quite as complex as I wanted her to be and not as well rounded. I actually found this with the majority of the characters in this book. We never got a real sense of who they were and what they were about. And not in a "ooo this is the mystery of it all" way but more of a "these characters are unfinished" kind of way. Not to mention Alexei, who is Russian and by default I must love him, was very disappointing as a chracter.<br /><br />I will be continuing with the series because I love the plotline that is going and based on the ending, I can see this opening wide up. However, I'm not sure if my feelings on the characters will change based on the fact that I think this is just how they are written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2957839585444373665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1131302900" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1131302900" />
    <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist"><img alt="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445582024p2/5383215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1131302900?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist">Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1131302900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12765750176853013567">This my first book by Ally Carter and although I wasn’t sure what to expect, I really liked All Fall Down. Even better, I’m really excited to read the next book! When I first heard about this book, I thought it would be a dystopia. But this is actually a contemporary/mystery. I must be really ignorant because I didn’t know that the Embassy Row is a real place in the United States. I’m not sure if this is exactly how it’s portrayed in the book since the book takes place in Adria and it seems like</span>
  <span id="freeText12765750176853013567" style="display:none">This my first book by Ally Carter and although I wasn’t sure what to expect, I really liked All Fall Down. Even better, I’m really excited to read the next book! When I first heard about this book, I thought it would be a dystopia. But this is actually a contemporary/mystery. I must be really ignorant because I didn’t know that the Embassy Row is a real place in the United States. I’m not sure if this is exactly how it’s portrayed in the book since the book takes place in Adria and it seems like it’s more than just buildings representing different countries because in this book you can be in the United States and take a few steps and technically you’re now in Russia. We also hear about shops in here and a lot of people and their families live on Embassy Row. I would have really liked to have seen a visualization or map of how the Embassy Row in the books is supposed to look like, because it sounds fascinating!<br><br>When her dad and brother are serving time in the military, Grace is sent back to live in Embassy Row with her grandfather who also happens to be the Ambassador for the United States. Being back in Adria means being back to the place where Grace’s mom was killed three years ago. A murder that she witnessed but that nobody will believe, no matter how many therapy sessions and meds she’s taken since then. Grace has a hard time being back in the place where her mother died at first, but when Noah assigns himself as Grace’s new best friend, things start looking up for Grace. She’s used to getting in trouble, but here in Embassy Row, getting into trouble can be a very dangerous thing. Despite the fact that, for the moment, all the embassies are in peace with each other, there is always this underlying tension. One wrong move can mean all-out-war. Grace is scared she will be that wrong move.<br><br>After being sure that the person who killed her mother is in Adria, Grace enlists the help of Noah, Megan and Rosie to help her catch the guy. But no matter how sure Grace is that her mother was killed and that her killer is ready to strike again, all the facts say that the fire that killed her mother was an accident. When Grace’s sanity and mental state are questioned, she doesn’t know who to trust or what is real and what is a made up memory. I really liked the mystery element of the story, always kept me guessing. I really liked the friendship between Grace and Noah and how that friendship eventually included Megan and Rosie, who were always willing to risk everything to help Grace. We also meet Alexei, Grace’s older brother’s longtime best friend and son of the Russian Ambassador. I wasn’t sure what to make of Alexei at first, is he the enemy, is he a potential love interest, or is he simply her brother’s best friend. I did love the few moments we got between them and wanted more. (I’m putting my money on him being the love interest). Grace was such a fun character. She was fearless and sarcastic and a little bit of a daredevil. But her not being able to trust her own mind or her memories, added a level of vulnerability that just made her more likable.<br><br>What kept me from loving this book, is that not only is there a lack of romance (which I’m okay with), but I’m not even sure who the love interest is supposed to be. We have Noah, the best friend who is determined to help out Grace find her mother’s killer. They spend a lot of time together and have a really great and playful friendship. But that was all I saw/felt between them. I NEVER once got the vibe that they like each other as more than friends or are even attracted to each other. Plus, most of the time, Noah is crushing on their friend Megan. But there are some readers who think he might be the love interest. Then we have Alexei who has this really complicated almost volatile relationship with Grace. She resents that Alexei is probably looking after her as a favor to her brother. She is mean to him sometimes (he knows how to dish it back) and they argue more than anything. But they was always this underlying tension and chemistry between them that I really liked. I wanted to see more of it, but Alexei rarely comes out. I’m about 80% sure Alexei is supposed to be the love interest (this doesn’t have a love triangle vibe to it, not yet at least) and if so, I think the romance part will be strong and worth the wait in the next book. I hope!<br><br>All Fall Down was a fun story with a unique premise that keeps you guessing with every new revelation. While I had guessed a few things (only because I always have a million theories) there were still some big things that took me by surprise. My favorite part of the book was the setting. OMG, the world created in Embassy Row was so damn fascinating! With the different embassies and properties and lands with their exotic shops and hidden underground tunnels, I fell in love with this setting. I’m sad that I have to wait so long for book 2 because I really want more!<br><br><b>4 out of 5 stars!</b><br><br>***<br><b>Read full review &amp; more of my reviews at <a href="http://www.mostlyyabookobsessed.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Mostly YA Book Obsessed</a></b><br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/albums/u367/nereyda1003/?action=view&amp;current=MyBlogSignature.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349417i/703417.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Follow me at:</b><br><b>

        <a title="Cora Tea Party Princess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cora Tea Party Princess" href="/user/show/4166936-cora-tea-party-princess">Cora Tea Party Princess</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer819190390464762451"><b>5 Words: Politics, family, death, memories, lies.</b><br/><br/>Having read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/56224.Ally_Carter' title='Ally Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ally Carter</a> before I was expecting action and intrigue and sass and teenage boys that act more like they're 25 than 15. I was not expecting this.<br/><br/>And I was actually a little bit disappointed.<br/><br/>It was a good read, a quick read, but it was rather slow in pace.   <span id="freeText819190390464762451" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: Politics, family, death, memories, lies.</b><br /><br />Having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/56224.Ally_Carter" title="Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Ally Carter</a> before I was expecting action and intrigue and sass and teenage boys that act more like they're 25 than 15. I was not expecting this.<br /><br />And I was actually a little bit disappointed.<br /><br />It was a good read, a quick read, but it was rather slow in pace. It felt like there was quite a bit of unnecessary filler in the pages. Even with this, a few of the characters just fell flat, 2D images hovering in the corner.<br /><br />There are teeny tiny hints at romance, but nothing you could really latch on to. I thought it was a bit of a shame, as even a little more development of these hints would have given the story more depth.<br /><br />All that said, I did enjoy this. And that twist at the end - the twist that I felt made the book - has made sure I'll read on. It hinted at all of the things I felt were missing and I can't wait.<br /><br />I loved how unreliable Grace was too, those last pages completely changed my perception of her. And it was very brave.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this for free via NetGalley for review purposes.</i></span>

  <span id="freeText1208022892844649087" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Hachette Children's Books and NetGalley.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“I can apologise in seven different languages. It’s just something you pick up when you’re me.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423854019i/13682835._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was an interesting YA mystery story, and I really liked the details revealed at the end of the book!<br><br>I liked Grace although she did make some questionable decisions at times. I felt really sorry for her in the way she’d lost her mother though, and it must have been really hard for her. Even though she came across as nuts, she really did have good intentions though, and was intent on finding her mother’s killer and bringing them to justice no matter what.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Yes, it was dark,” I snap back. “Yes, I was young, and it was traumatic. Yes, I have never been the most reliable girl in the world, but I know what I saw. And I’m telling you, I saw a man with a scar on his left cheek shoot my mother. I heard the bomb that burned her shop to the ground.”</i>

Grace’s questionable decisions actually made for some amusing situations, and Grace came out with some brilliant lines, and she really made me laugh!<br><br><b>
  <i>“Oh my gosh,” I mutter to myself. “That guy is hot.”<br>“That guy’s my dad.” Noah says it like he’s said it like he’s said it a lot. “The ambassador.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400845882ra/9727185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were some things that I didn’t really understand, because I don’t know anything about international relations, but I managed to get the gist of it.<br><br><b>
  <i>“It’s not like it’s an international incident.” I look from Lila to Megan to Rosie, and then finally I let my gaze linger on Noah, who eases closer, lowers his voice.<br>“Actually, Grace, it kind of is. We’re Israeli. And that is Iran.”<br>When I look back at the blue-and-white scarf, I realise that, from a distance, it bears a striking resemblance to the flag of Lila and Noah’s home nation.<br>“The Israeli ambassador gave that scarf to our mom. In fact, he gave scarves like it to all of the women on his senior staff,” Noah says. “If anyone sees that up there…”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423854019i/13682836.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was interesting, and I liked the details that were revealed. I did guess one thing very early on, but I didn’t guess the rest, and I did enjoy this book overall.<br>7.25 out of 10<br><br><b>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1213668992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16222324406268680358">I read <i>All Fall Down</i> as a buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16406648-kathy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kathy</a> from <a href='https://thenoveltyoflife.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Novelty of Life</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16411696-cassandra-caruso' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cassandra</a> from <a href='https://m.youtube.com/channel/UCz3zbb8PdLLd1OEq0IMPxsw' rel='nofollow noopener'>ccbooks66512</a>. Overall, I found it to be a combination of mildly intriguing and tremendously frustrating, and I seem to be struggling to rate it (I apologize to those of you who have been watching me change the rating back and forth between two and three stars for the past hour).  I’ve finally settled on two stars and am trying to restrain myself from making any further changes.  <br/><br/>Grace is an army brat, nev</span>
  <span id="freeText16222324406268680358" style="display:none">I read <i>All Fall Down</i> as a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16406648-kathy" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathy</a> from <a href="https://thenoveltyoflife.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Novelty of Life</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16411696-cassandra-caruso" rel="nofollow noopener">Cassandra</a> from <a href="https://m.youtube.com/channel/UCz3zbb8PdLLd1OEq0IMPxsw" rel="nofollow noopener">ccbooks66512</a>. Overall, I found it to be a combination of mildly intriguing and tremendously frustrating, and I seem to be struggling to rate it (I apologize to those of you who have been watching me change the rating back and forth between two and three stars for the past hour).  I’ve finally settled on two stars and am trying to restrain myself from making any further changes.  <br /><br />Grace is an army brat, never settling in one area for an extended period of time.  She’s also the granddaughter of a U.S. ambassador, spending each summer at Embassy Row alongside other children her age.  This summer, however, Embassy Row isn’t characterized by the usual fun, carefree attitude.  Instead, it serves as a vivid reminder for Grace of her mother’s death.  Having witnessed the traumatic incident, Grace is convinced that her mother was murdered at the hands of a frightening man with a jagged scar across his face.  Afterward, however, Grace is told that her mother’s death was accidental due to smoke inhalation.  Refusing to discredit her memories of the event, Grace remains adamant that her mother’s death was no accident. <blockquote>
  <i>“Yes, it was dark,” I snap back. “Yes, I was young, and it was traumatic. Yes, I have never been the most reliable girl in the world, but I know what I saw. And I’m telling you, I saw a man with a scar on his left cheek shoot my mother. I heard the bomb that burned her shop to the ground.” </i>
</blockquote>She undergoes years of psychiatric treatment but is unable to forget the incident.  When she returns to Embassy Row for the summer, she realizes that there may be more going on than what initially meets the eye.  Deciding to dig a little deeper into a series of mysterious occurrences, Grace realizes that she must choose her friends carefully.<br /><br />I wasn’t immediately hooked when I began reading - the first 150 pages were very slow and a bit heavy on the political interactions between countries.  Having minimal knowledge about international relations, I found these sections to be particularly boring, and I ended up skimming most of them.  Midway through the book, however, the action picked up significantly, but seemed to fade away, only to reappear in fits and starts.  The resulting, unpleasant lurching speed of the plot left a little to be desired, but this was made up for by a few plot twists that I certainly did not see coming (I don't want to elaborate any further because it would make this review quite spoiler-heavy).<br /><br />This was my second foray into Ally Carter’s writing - I read I’d Tell You I Loved You But Then I’d Have to Kill You about a year ago, and that went over like a lead balloon, full rant <a href="https://brewingupbooks.wordpress.com/2015/01/02/review-id-tell-you-i-love-you-but-then-id-have-to-kill-you/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.  But I allowed someone to convince me to give her books another chance, and I still wasn’t overwhelmingly impressed.  Once again, I found that Carter’s writing style was geared more toward a younger audience (although this could simply be me “outgrowing” young adult books).  I thought the plot was oversimplified - it could have been much more complex and likely would have better held my attention.<br /><br />On a similar note, there wasn't much character development throughout the course of the novel.  The main characters in particular were extremely static, changing minimally, if at all.  Grace, who served as the first person narrator, shed a very immature light on events as they unfolded, failing to consider the consequences of her actions or to view a situation from someone else's perspective.  I would generally associate such a trait with a more juvenile character, but seeing as Grace was nearly a legal adult, I found the characteristic to be a bit out of place.  She also had a tendency to assume a whiny tone and mental attitude when things didn't go precisely her way.  I did not realize that I would be dealing with a tempermental toddler when I began reading.<br /><br />As the narrative continued, it became increasingly difficult to distinguish between flashbacks and hallucinations.  While this was likely intentional, it became a bit confusing to the point that I was forced to reread several chapters simply to decipher when said events were occuring. Consequently, Grace was a fairly unreliable narrator - it was nearly impossible at times to differentiate between reality and Grace's twisted yet not entirely truthful perception of a situation. <br /><br />The secondary characters shared one thing in common: they all lacked back stories.  Perhaps this is something that will be addressed in later books in the series, but they all felt like flat, lifeless pieces of cardboard to me.  It would have been nice to learn a bit about the past, particularly since Grace's recollection of it is so jumbled. <br /><br />The romantic aspect of the novel is where it starts to get a little tricky - while there are two male characters with close relationships to Grace, there is <b>no love triangle</b> (which is a huge relief, at least in my book). Alexei, who lives in the Russian sector of Embassy Row served as Grace's brother's best friend and an older brother figure for Grace, always looking out for her and keeping her best interests in mind. Noah, on the other hand, serves as more of a romantic interest throughout the novel...but nothing happens between Grace and Noah. Whatsoever. Leaving me enraged and extremely disappointed (which is never a good combination).  <br /><br />While I commend Carter for her originality and perseverance in regard to her writing, I found myself unable to move past several components of this book. Between the characters, plot, and pacing, I found this book turned reading into a chore - I was determined to complete the novel in the hopes of some magical, drastic improvement in these respects, but to no avail. I had fairly high hopes for All Fall Down, and while it didn't meet many of my expectations, my nagging curiosity will likely prompt me to continue on with the series. And who knows, I may be pleasantly surprised with the remainder of the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16222324406268680358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
